## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: classical mechanics (nonlinear oscillations / dynamical systems)
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration expressed as a function of position x, velocity v, and possibly explicit time t, which is the standard state-space form of (non)linear oscillators. Common physical effects are restoring forces from a potential (depend on x), dissipation (depend on v), and external/parametric forcing (depend on t and/or x,t).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear undamped oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (small-amplitude Hookean restoring force; sign of c0 typically negative)
- Linear viscous damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (damped harmonic oscillator in first-order form)
- Quadratic drag damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * Abs(v) (aerodynamic-like drag in oscillatory motion)
- Coulomb (dry) friction damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * Sign(v) (sliding friction dominated dissipation)
- Duffing oscillator (cubic stiffness): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (hardening/softening spring plus damping)
- Quintic stiffness extension: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 + c3 * v (stronger nonlinearity at large amplitude)
- Nonlinear damping (amplitude-dependent dissipation): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * x**2 * v (damping increases with displacement amplitude)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (c2 - x**2) * v (self-excited oscillations / limit cycle via negative damping near origin)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (c2 - v**2) * v (self-excitation controlled by velocity-dependent damping)
- Driven oscillator (additive forcing): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t + c4) (external periodic drive)
- Parametrically excited oscillator: dv_dt = (c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x + c3 * v (time-varying stiffness; Mathieu-type behavior)
- Nonlinear restoring force saturation: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x / (x**2 + c2) + c3 * v (restoring force weakens/levels off at large |x|)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Conservative restoring force from a potential: dv_dt depends only on x and is odd in x (e.g., c0*x + c1*x**3), indicating energy exchange between x and v without dissipation.
- Viscous dissipation: terms proportional to v (or higher odd powers of v) remove energy; coefficients typically yield dv_dt opposing v.
- Quadratic drag signature: v*Abs(v) appears when damping scales with speed squared while preserving direction opposing motion.
- Self-excited/limit-cycle behavior: factors like (c - x**2)*v or (c - v**2)*v imply negative damping at small amplitude and positive damping at large amplitude.
- Hardening vs softening stiffness: a positive vs negative cubic term in x**3 changes how oscillation frequency shifts with amplitude.
- External periodic driving: explicit sin(c*t+phi) or cos(c*t) terms introduce resonance/entrainment and break time-translation invariance.
- Parametric resonance: time-modulation multiplying x (e.g., (c0+c1*cos(c2*t))*x) indicates stiffness modulation rather than additive forcing.
- Dry friction effects: Sign(v) (often with a constant magnitude) creates stick-slip and nonsmooth dynamics near v=0.
- Amplitude-dependent damping: x**2*v (or higher even-in-x times v) indicates dissipation that grows with displacement amplitude, common in structural/nonlinear materials.

Key basis functions in GT:
1. `x³` (polynomial)
2. `sin(t)` (trigonometric in t)
3. `v*sin(x)` (product of v and sin(x))
4. `sin(v)` (trigonometric in v)

The GT has nonlinear functions of both `x` and `v`: `sin(x)` and `sin(v)`. This is crucial - most candidates use polynomial/linear terms in v and x, which cannot replicate `sin(x)` or `sin(v)` exactly.

Let me analyze each candidate:

**Candidates 1, 7-29, 47-49:** These contain terms like `c*v`, `c*x`, `c*x³`, trigonometric functions of `t` only, and polynomial combinations of `x` and `v`. None contain `sin(x)` or `sin(v)`. Since `v*sin(x)` and `sin(v)` cannot be represented by polynomials in `x` and `v`, these are all **NO MATCH**.

**Candidates 2-6:** Similar - contain `x³*exp(c*v)`, `v*|v|`, polynomial terms, `sin(t)`, but no `sin(x)` or `sin(v)`. **NO MATCH**.
